<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
147</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mechanism-of-action-of-antipsychotic-drugs">MECHANISM OF ACTION OF ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanism-of-action-of-antipsychotic-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The major action of all antipsychotics in the nervous system is to block receptors for the neurotransmitter dopamine.</li>
<li>The typical antipsychotic drugs are potent antagonists (blockers) of dopamine receptors D2, D3, and D4.</li>
<li>This makes them effective in treating target symptoms but also produces many extrapyramidal side effects.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
148</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mechanism-of-action-of-antipsychotic-drugs">MECHANISM OF ACTION OF ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanism-of-action-of-antipsychotic-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Newer, atypical antipsychotic drugs, such as clozapine (Clozaril), are relatively weak blockers of D2, which may account for the lower incidence of extrapyramidal side effects.</li>
<li>Atypical antipsychotics also inhibit the reuptake of serotonin, which makes them more effective in treating the depressive aspects of Schizophrenia</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
149</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects-of-antipsychotic-drugs">SIDE EFFECTS OF ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-of-antipsychotic-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Review pyramidal vs extrapyramidal tracts.</li>
<li>Extrapyramidal Symptoms (EPS) are serious neurologic symptoms that are the major side effects of antipsychotic drugs, which include:</li>
<li>Acute Dystonia</li>
<li>Pseudoparkinsonism</li>
<li>Akathisia</li>
<li>Tardive Dyskinesia</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
150</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="e464aa4d">SIDE EFFECTS OF ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS – EXTRAPYRAMIDAL SYMPTOMS (EPS)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#e464aa4d" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Blockade of D2 receptors in the midbrain region of the brain stem is responsible for the development of EPS</li>
<li>Therapies for the neurologic side effects of acute dystonia, pseudoparkinsonism, and akathisia are similar and include:</li>
<li>
<ol>
<li>Lowering the dosage of the antipsychotic</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="2">
<li>Changing to a different antipsychotic</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="3">
<li>Administering anticholinergic medication</li>
</ol>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
151</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drugs-used-to-treat-extrapyramidal-side-effects">DRUGS USED TO TREAT EXTRAPYRAMIDAL SIDE EFFECTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drugs-used-to-treat-extrapyramidal-side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drugs-used-to-treat-extrapyramidal-side-effects">DRUGS USED TO TREAT EXTRAPYRAMIDAL SIDE EFFECTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drugs-used-to-treat-extrapyramidal-side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>GENERIC (TRADE) NAME</th><th>ORAL DOSAGES (mg)</th><th>IM / IV DOSES (mg)</th><th>DRUG CLASS</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Lorazepam (Ativan)</td><td>1 – 2 tid</td><td>-</td><td>Benzodiazepine</td></tr><tr><td>Procyclidine (Kemadrin)</td><td>2.5 – 5 tid</td><td>-</td><td>Anticholinergic</td></tr><tr><td>Propranolol (Inderal)</td><td>10 – 20 tid; up to 40 qid</td><td>-</td><td>Beta-blocker</td></tr><tr><td>Trihexaphenidyl (Artane)</td><td>2 – 5 tid</td><td>-</td><td>Anticholinergic</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="70bcc8fe">SIDE EFFECTS OF ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS – (EPS) – ACUTE DYSTONIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#70bcc8fe" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This includes any of the following:</li>
<li>Acute muscular rigidity and cramping</li>
<li>A stiff or thick tongue with difficulty of swallowing</li>
<li>In severe cases, laryngospasm and respiratory difficulties.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
154</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects-of-antipsychotic-drugs-eps-acute-dystonia">SIDE EFFECTS OF ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS - (EPS) - ACUTE DYSTONIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-of-antipsychotic-drugs-eps-acute-dystonia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-045cb698.jpeg" alt="img-26.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>Spasms or stiffness in muscle groups can produce torticollis (twisted head and neck)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
155</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects-of-antipsychotic-drugs-eps-acute-dystonia">SIDE EFFECTS OF ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS - (EPS) - ACUTE DYSTONIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-of-antipsychotic-drugs-eps-acute-dystonia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-e0eff622.jpeg" alt="img-27.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>Spasms or stiffness in muscle groups can produce opisthotonus (tightness in the entire body with the head back and an arched neck)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
156</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects-of-antipsychotic-drugs-eps-acute-dystonia">SIDE EFFECTS OF ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS - (EPS) - ACUTE DYSTONIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-of-antipsychotic-drugs-eps-acute-dystonia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-884b2461.jpeg" alt="img-28.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>Spasms or stiffness in muscle groups can produce an oculogyric crisis (eyes rolled back in a locked position)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
157</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment-for-eps-acute-dystonia">TREATMENT FOR (EPS) ACUTE DYSTONIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-for-eps-acute-dystonia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Rapid relief is brought about by immediate treatment with anticholinergic drugs such as:</li>
<li>Intramuscular benztropine mesylate (Cogentin)</li>
<li>Intramuscular or intravenous diphenhydramine (Benadryl)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
158</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment-for-eps-acute-dystonia">TREATMENT FOR (EPS) ACUTE DYSTONIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-for-eps-acute-dystonia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Recurrent dystonic reactions would necessitate a lower dosage or a change in the antipsychotic drug.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
159</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects-of-antipsychotic-drugs-eps-pseudoparkinsonism">SIDE EFFECTS OF ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS - (EPS) - PSEUDOPARKINSONISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-of-antipsychotic-drugs-eps-pseudoparkinsonism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Drug-induced Parkinsonism or pseudoparkinsonism have the following symptoms:</li>
<li>A stiff, stooped posture</li>
<li>Masklike facies</li>
<li>Decreased arm swing</li>
<li>A shuffling, festinating gait (with small steps)</li>
<li>Cogwheel rigidity (ratchet-like movements of joints)</li>
<li>Drooling</li>
<li>Tremor</li>
<li>Bradycardia</li>
<li>Coarse pill-rolling movements of the thumb and fingers while at rest</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
160</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment-for-eps-pseudoparkinsonism">TREATMENT FOR (EPS) PSEUDOPARKINSONISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-for-eps-pseudoparkinsonism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Pseudoparkinsonism is treated by changing to an antipsychotic medication that has a lower incidence of EPS or by adding an oral anticholinergic agent or amantadine.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
161</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="153fd6f7">SIDE EFFECTS OF ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS – (EPS) – AKATHISIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#153fd6f7" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Akathisia is reported by the client as an intense need to move about</li>
<li>The client appears restless or anxious and agitated, often with a rigid posture or gait and a lack of spontaneous gestures.</li>
<li>This feeling of internal restlessness and the inability to sit still or rest often leads clients to discontinue their antipsychotic medication.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
162</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment-for-eps-akathisia">TREATMENT FOR (EPS) AKATHISIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-for-eps-akathisia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Akathisia can be treated by a change in antipsychotic medication or the addition of an oral agent such as a beta-blocker, anticholinergic, or benzodiazepine.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
163</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6a9dc7aa">SIDE EFFECTS OF ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS – (EPS) – TARDIVE DYSKINESIA (TD)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6a9dc7aa" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>TD is a syndrome of permanent, involuntary movements, is most commonly caused by the long-term use of typical antipsychotics.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Once it has developed, TD is irreversible.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Symptoms of TD include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Involuntary movements of the tongue, facial and neck muscles, upper and lower extremities, and truncal musculature</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tongue-thrusting and protrusion, lip-smacking, blinking, grimacing and other excessive, unnecessary facial movements</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
164</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment-for-eps-tardive-dyskinesia">TREATMENT FOR (EPS) TARDIVE DYSKINESIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-for-eps-tardive-dyskinesia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Although TD is irreversible, its progression can be arrested by decreasing or discontinuing the antipsychotic medication.</li>
<li>Preventing the occurrence of TD is done by keeping maintenance dosages as low as possible, changing medications, and monitoring the client periodically for the initial signs of TD.</li>
<li>Persons who have already developed signs of TD but who still need to take antipsychotic medication are often given clozapine, which has not yet been found to cause, or therefore worsen, TD.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
165</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="other-side-effects-of-antipsychotic-drugs">OTHER SIDE EFFECTS OF ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-side-effects-of-antipsychotic-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Neuroleptic Malignant Syndrome</li>
<li>Anticholinergic Side Effects</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
166</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7dea8549">SIDE EFFECTS OF ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS – NEUROLEPTIC MALIGNANT SYNDROME (NMS)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7dea8549" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>NMS is a potentially fatal, idiosyncratic reaction to an antipsychotic drug with the following symptoms:</li>
<li>Rigidity</li>
<li>High fever</li>
<li>Autonomic instability such as unstable blood pressure, diaphoresis, pallor, delirium and elevated levels of enzymes (particularly CPK).</li>
<li>Confusion</li>
<li>Being mute</li>
<li>Fluctuation from agitation to stupor</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
167</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7dea8549">SIDE EFFECTS OF ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS – NEUROLEPTIC MALIGNANT SYNDROME (NMS)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7dea8549" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Dehydration, poor nutrition, and concurrent medical illness all increase the risk for NMS.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
168</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment-for-neuroleptic-malignant-syndrome-nms">TREATMENT FOR NEUROLEPTIC MALIGNANT SYNDROME (NMS)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-for-neuroleptic-malignant-syndrome-nms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This includes the following:</li>
<li>Immediate discontinuance of all antipsychotic medications</li>
<li>Institution of supportive medical care such as rehydration and hypothermia, until the client's physical condition is stabilized.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
169</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1acede3d">SIDE EFFECTS OF ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS – ANTICHOLINERGIC SIDE EFFECTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1acede3d" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms usually decrease after 3 – 4 weeks but do not entirely remit and include the following:</li>
<li>Orthostatic hypotension</li>
<li>Dry mouth</li>
<li>Constipation</li>
<li>Urinary hesitance or retention</li>
<li>Blurred near vision</li>
<li>Dry eyes</li>
<li>Photophobia</li>
<li>Nasal congestion</li>
<li>Decreased memory</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
170</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment-for-anticholinergic-side-effects">TREATMENT FOR ANTICHOLINERGIC SIDE EFFECTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-for-anticholinergic-side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The client who is taking anticholinergic agents for EPS may have increased problems with anticholinergic side effects, but some nutritional or over-the-counter remedies can ease these symptoms</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
171</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="client-teaching-and-medication-management-antipsychotic-drugs">CLIENT TEACHING AND MEDICATION MANAGEMENT: ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#client-teaching-and-medication-management-antipsychotic-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Drink sugar-free fluids and eat sugar-free hard candy to ease the anticholinergic effects of dry mouth.</li>
<li>Avoid calorie-laden beverages and candy because they promote dental caries, contribute to weight gain, and do little to relieve dry mouth.</li>
<li>Constipation can be prevented or relieved by increasing intake of water and bulk-forming foods in the diet and by exercising.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
172</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="client-teaching-and-medication-management-antipsychotic-drugs">CLIENT TEACHING AND MEDICATION MANAGEMENT: ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#client-teaching-and-medication-management-antipsychotic-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Stool softeners are permissible, but laxatives should be avoided.</li>
<li>Use sunscreen to prevent burning and avoid long periods of time in the sun. Wear protective clothing as photosensitivity can cause a patient to burn easily.</li>
<li>Rising slowly from a sitting or lying position will prevent falls from orthostatic hypotension or dizziness due to a drop in blood pressure. Wait to walk until any dizziness has subsided.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
173</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="client-teaching-and-medication-management-antipsychotic-drugs">CLIENT TEACHING AND MEDICATION MANAGEMENT: ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#client-teaching-and-medication-management-antipsychotic-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Monitor the amount of sleepiness or drowsiness you experience. Avoid driving a car or performing other potentially dangerous activities until your response time and reflexes seem normal.</li>
<li>If you forget a dose of antipsychotic medication, take it if the dose is only 3 to 4 hours late. If the missed dose is more than 4 hours late or the next dose is due, omit the forgotten dose.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
174</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="client-teaching-and-medication-management-antipsychotic-drugs">CLIENT TEACHING AND MEDICATION MANAGEMENT: ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#client-teaching-and-medication-management-antipsychotic-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>If you have difficulty remembering your medication, use a chart to record doses when taken, or use a pill box labeled with dosage times and/or days of the week to help you remember when to take medication.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
175</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1a8c028d">SIDE EFFECTS OF ATYPICAL ANTIPSYCHOTIC DRUGS – CLOZAPINE (Clozaril)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1a8c028d" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This drug produces fewer traditional side effects than most typical antipsychotic drugs, but it has the potentially fatal side effect of agranulocytosis.</li>
<li>This develops suddenly and is characterized by fever, malaise, ulcerative sore throat, and leukopenia.</li>
<li>This side effect can occur up to 24 weeks after the initiation of therapy</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
176</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment-of-agranulocytosis-due-to-clozapine-clozaril">TREATMENT OF AGRANULOCYTOSIS DUE TO CLOZAPINE (Clozaril)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-agranulocytosis-due-to-clozapine-clozaril" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Blood samples should be taken weekly to monitor the WBC count of patients with agranulocytosis.</li>
<li>The drug must be discontinued immediately if the white blood cell count drops by 50% or to less than 3,000.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
177</p>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
178</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-antidepressant-drugs">2) ANTIDEPRESSANT DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-antidepressant-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="antidepressant-drugs">ANTIDEPRESSANT DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antidepressant-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Antidepressant drugs are primarily used in the treatment of:</li>
<li>Major depressive illness</li>
<li>Panic disorder</li>
<li>Other anxiety disorders</li>
<li>Bipolar depression</li>
<li>Psychotic depression</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
179</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="antidepressant-drugs">ANTIDEPRESSANT DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antidepressant-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Although the mechanism of action is not completely understood, antidepressants somehow interact with two neurotransmitters,</li>
<li>norepinephrine and</li>
<li>serotonin,</li>
<li>that regulate mood, arousal, attention, memory processing and appetite</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
180</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mechanism-of-action-of-antidepressant-drugs">MECHANISM OF ACTION OF ANTIDEPRESSANT DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanism-of-action-of-antidepressant-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The cyclic antidepressants and venlafaxine block the reuptake of norepinephrine primarily and serotonin to some degree.</li>
<li>The Monoamine Oxidase Inhibitors (MAOIs) interfere with enzyme metabolism.</li>
<li>The Selective Serotonin Reuptake Inhibitors (SSRIs) block the reuptake of serotonin</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
181</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects-of-cyclic-antidepressant-drugs">SIDE EFFECTS OF CYCLIC ANTIDEPRESSANT DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-of-cyclic-antidepressant-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The cyclic antidepressant drugs block cholinergic receptors, resulting in anticholinergic effects such as:</li>
<li>Dry mouth</li>
<li>Constipation</li>
<li>Urinary hesitancy or retention</li>
<li>Dry nasal passages</li>
<li>Blurred near vision</li>
<li>Agitation, delirium and ileus are more severe anticholinergic side effects that may occur in the elderly.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
182</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects-of-cyclic-antidepressant-drugs">SIDE EFFECTS OF CYCLIC ANTIDEPRESSANT DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-of-cyclic-antidepressant-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Other common side effects include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Orthostatic hypotension</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sedation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Weight gain</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tachycardia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sexual dysfunction is frequently reported by clients taking TCAs</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
183</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2b-monoamine-oxidase-inhibitor-maoi-antidepressant-drugs">2B) MONOAMINE OXIDASE INHIBITOR (MAOI) ANTIDEPRESSANT DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2b-monoamine-oxidase-inhibitor-maoi-antidepressant-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
184</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects-of-monoamine-oxidase-inhibitors-maois">SIDE EFFECTS OF MONOAMINE OXIDASE INHIBITORS (MAOIs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-of-monoamine-oxidase-inhibitors-maois" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The most common side effects of MAOIs include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Day-time sedation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Insomnia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Weight gain</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dry mouth</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Orthostatic hypotension</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sexual dysfunction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sedation and insomnia are difficult to treat and may necessitate a change in medication</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
185</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects-of-monoamine-oxidase-inhibitors-maois">SIDE EFFECTS OF MONOAMINE OXIDASE INHIBITORS (MAOIs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-of-monoamine-oxidase-inhibitors-maois" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Of particular concern with MAOIs is the potential for a life-threatening hypertensive crisis if the client ingests food containing tyramine.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The symptoms of this crisis are:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Severe hypertension</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hyperpyrexia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tachycardia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diaphoresis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tremulousness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cardiac Arrythmias</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
186</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="foods-containing-tyramine-to-avoid-when-taking-monoamine-oxidase-inhibitors-maois">FOODS (CONTAINING TYRAMINE) TO AVOID WHEN TAKING MONOAMINE OXIDASE INHIBITORS (MAOIs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#foods-containing-tyramine-to-avoid-when-taking-monoamine-oxidase-inhibitors-maois" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>No mature or aged cheeses or dishes made with cheese, such as lasagna, pizza. All cheese is considered aged except cottage cheese, cream cheese, ricotta cheese, and processed cheese slices</li>
<li>No aged meats such as pepperoni, salami, mortadella, summer sausage, beef logs, and similar products. Make sure meat and chicken are fresh and have been properly refrigerated.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
187</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="monoamine-oxidase-inhibitors-drug-interaction-drug-alert">MONOAMINE OXIDASE INHIBITORS DRUG INTERACTION - DRUG ALERT!!!<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#monoamine-oxidase-inhibitors-drug-interaction-drug-alert" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The following drugs can cause a potentially fatal drug interaction when taken with MAOI antidepressants:</p>
<ul>
<li>Other MAOI antidepressants</li>
<li>SSRI antidepressants</li>
<li>Certain cyclic compounds</li>
<li>Meperidine (Demerol)</li>
<li>Buspirone (BuSpar)</li>
<li>Dextromethorphan</li>
<li>General anesthetic</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
188</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2c-selective-serotonin-reuptake-inhibitor-ssri-antidepressant-drugs">2C) SELECTIVE SEROTONIN REUPTAKE INHIBITOR (SSRI) ANTIDEPRESSANT DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2c-selective-serotonin-reuptake-inhibitor-ssri-antidepressant-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
189</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects-of-selective-serotonin-reuptake-inhibitors-ssris">SIDE EFFECTS OF SELECTIVE SEROTONIN REUPTAKE INHIBITORS (SSRIs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-of-selective-serotonin-reuptake-inhibitors-ssris" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Less common side effects include:</li>
<li>Sedation particularly with paroxetine or Paxil (indicates need for a change to another antidepressant)</li>
<li>Sweating (indicates need for change to another antidepressant)</li>
<li>Diarrhea (manage with symptomatic treatment)</li>
<li>Hand tremor</li>
<li>Headaches (manage with symptomatic treatment)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
190</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drug-interactions-for-selective-serotonin-reuptake-inhibitors-ssris">DRUG INTERACTIONS FOR SELECTIVE SEROTONIN REUPTAKE INHIBITORS (SSRIs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-interactions-for-selective-serotonin-reuptake-inhibitors-ssris" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>An uncommon but potentially serious drug interaction called serotonin or serotonergic syndrome can result from taking a MAOI and an SSRI at the same time</li>
<li>It can also occur if one of these drugs is taken too close to the end of therapy with the other</li>
<li>Therefore, one drug must clear the person's system before therapy with the other drug is initiated</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
191</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drug-interactions-for-selective-serotonin-reuptake-inhibitors-ssris">DRUG INTERACTIONS FOR SELECTIVE SEROTONIN REUPTAKE INHIBITORS (SSRIs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-interactions-for-selective-serotonin-reuptake-inhibitors-ssris" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms of the serotonergic syndrome include:</li>
<li>Agitation</li>
<li>Sweating</li>
<li>Fever</li>
<li>Tachycardia</li>
<li>Hypotention</li>
<li>Rigidity</li>
<li>Hyperreflexia</li>
<li>In extreme reactions, even coma and death could occur.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
192</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="client-teaching-and-medication-management-antidepressant-drugs">CLIENT TEACHING AND MEDICATION MANAGEMENT: ANTIDEPRESSANT DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#client-teaching-and-medication-management-antidepressant-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Minimize nausea by taking medication with food.</li>
<li>To reduce insomnia, take daily doses in the morning. If this is not effective, ask the physician if a medication for sleep is indicated. Do not use alcohol to induce sleep, because this will worsen insomnia.</li>
<li>For diarrhea and headaches caused by the medication, take over-the-counter medications approved by the physician.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
193</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="client-teaching-and-medication-management-antidepressant-drugs">CLIENT TEACHING AND MEDICATION MANAGEMENT: ANTIDEPRESSANT DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#client-teaching-and-medication-management-antidepressant-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Initial sedation effects generally lessen with time. If they persist, talk to the physician about modifying the dose or changing medications</li>
<li>For motor restlessness or hand tremor, ask the physician for a medication such as propranolol (Inderal) or a benzodiazepine</li>
<li>Use calorie-free beverages or sugar-free candy to relieve dry mouth. Avoid calorie-laden beverages, because they do not alleviate dry mouth and may add to weight gain.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
194</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="client-teaching-and-medication-management-antidepressant-drugs">CLIENT TEACHING AND MEDICATION MANAGEMENT: ANTIDEPRESSANT DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#client-teaching-and-medication-management-antidepressant-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Try to get a balanced diet to avoid excess weight gain. Exercise is also beneficial.</li>
<li>Increase your intake of water and bulk-forming foods to prevent or relieve constipation. Stool softeners are permitted. But laxatives should be avoided.</li>
<li>Do not drink alcohol while taking antidepressants</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
195</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="client-teaching-and-medication-management-antidepressant-drugs">CLIENT TEACHING AND MEDICATION MANAGEMENT: ANTIDEPRESSANT DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#client-teaching-and-medication-management-antidepressant-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>If problems with sexual drive or having an erection or orgasm occur, discuss them with the physician rather than altering or stopping medication. Other antidepressants may be appropriate.</li>
<li>If you miss a dose of the drug, follow the directions given by your physician.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
196</p>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
197</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-mood-stabilizing-drugs">3) MOOD STABILIZING DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-mood-stabilizing-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mood-stabilizing-drugs">MOOD STABILIZING DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mood-stabilizing-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These are used for the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>To treat bipolar affective disorder by stabilizing the client's mood</li>
<li>To avoid or minimize the highs and lows that characterize bipolar illness</li>
<li>To treat the acute phases of mania</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
198</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mood-stabilizing-drugs">MOOD STABILIZING DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mood-stabilizing-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Lithium is the most established mood stabilizer</li>
<li>Some anticonvulsant drugs are effective mood stabilizers such as:</li>
<li>Carbamazepine (Tegretol)</li>
<li>Valproic Acid (Depakene, Depakote)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
199</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mood-stabilizing-drugs">MOOD STABILIZING DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mood-stabilizing-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Other anticonvulsants, such as gabapentin (Neurontin) and lamotrigine (Lamictal), are being used on a trial basis for mood stabilization</li>
<li>Occasionally, clonazepam (Klonopin), an anti-anxiety agent, is also used to treat acute mania.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
200</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mechanism-of-action-of-mood-stabilizing-drugs">MECHANISM OF ACTION OF MOOD STABILIZING DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanism-of-action-of-mood-stabilizing-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Lithium normalizes the reuptake of certain neurotransmitters, such as:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Serotonin</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Norepinephrine</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Acetylcholine</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dopamine</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lithium also reduces the release of norepinephrine through competition with calcium</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lithium produces its effects intracellularly rather than within neuronal synapses.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
201</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dosage-of-mood-stabilizing-drugs-lithium">DOSAGE OF MOOD STABILIZING DRUGS - LITHIUM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dosage-of-mood-stabilizing-drugs-lithium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Lithium is available in tablets, capsules, liquid and a sustained release form but NO PARENTERAL FORMS ARE AVAILABLE.</li>
<li>Daily dosages generally range from 900 mg to 3,600 mg.</li>
<li>More importantly, the serum Lithium level should be about 1.0 mEq/L</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
202</p>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
203</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="4-antianxiety-drugs-anxiolytics">4) ANTIANXIETY DRUGS (ANXIOLYTICS)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-antianxiety-drugs-anxiolytics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="drug-alert-benzodiazepines">DRUG ALERT!!! - BENZODIAZEPINES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-alert-benzodiazepines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Benzodiazepines strongly enhance the effects of alcohol</li>
<li>Clients should not drink alcohol when taking benzodiazepines, or indeed any psychotropic drug.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
204</p>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
205</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="5-stimulants">5) STIMULANTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-stimulants" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stimulant-drugs">STIMULANT DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stimulant-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The primary drugs used to treat ADHD are the CNS stimulants:</li>
<li>methylphenidate (Ritalin)</li>
<li>pemoline (Cylert)</li>
<li>dextroamphetamine (Dexedrine)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
206</p>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
207</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6-sensitizing-drugs">6) SENSITIZING DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-sensitizing-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="disulfiram-antabuse">DISULFIRAM (ANTABUSE)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disulfiram-antabuse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Disulfiram is a sensitizing agent that causes an adverse reaction when mixed with alcohol in the body.</li>
<li>This agent's only use is as a deterrent to drinking alcohol in persons receiving treatment for alcoholism.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
208</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="adverse-reaction-when-disulfiram-antabuse-mixes-with-alcohol">ADVERSE REACTION WHEN DISULFIRAM (ANTABUSE) MIXES WITH ALCOHOL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adverse-reaction-when-disulfiram-antabuse-mixes-with-alcohol" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Five to ten minutes after someone who is taking disulfiram ingests alcohol, symptoms begin to appear:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Facial and body flushing from vasodilation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A throbbing headache</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sweating</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dry mouth</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nausea and vomiting</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dizziness and weakness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In severe cases, severe hypotension, confusion and even death.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Symptoms progress rapidly and last from 30 minutes to 2 hours.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
209</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mechanism-of-action-of-disulfiram-antabuse">MECHANISM OF ACTION OF DISULFIRAM (ANTABUSE)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanism-of-action-of-disulfiram-antabuse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Disulfiram inhibits the enzyme aldehyde dehydrogenase, which is involved in the metabolism of ethanol.</li>
<li>Acetaldehyde levels are then increased from 5 to 10 times higher than normal, resulting in the disulfiram-alcohol reaction</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
210</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects-of-disulfiram-antabuse">SIDE EFFECTS OF DISULFIRAM (ANTABUSE)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-of-disulfiram-antabuse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Side effects of taking Disulfiram include:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fatigue</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Drowsiness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Halitosis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tremor</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Impotence</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It can interfere with the metabolism of other drugs the client is taking such as: phenytoin (Dilantin), isoniazid (INH), warfarin (Coumadin), barbiturates, and long-acting benzodiazepines such as diazepam and chlordiazepoxide.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
211</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="client-education-for-patients-taking-disulfiram-antabuse">CLIENT EDUCATION FOR PATIENTS TAKING DISULFIRAM (ANTABUSE)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#client-education-for-patients-taking-disulfiram-antabuse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Many common products contain alcohol, such as:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Shaving cream</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Aftershave lotion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cologne</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Deodorant</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Over-the-counter medications such as cough preparations</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When used by the client taking disulfiram, these products can produce the same reaction as drinking alcohol</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The client must read product labels carefully and select items that are alcohol-free</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
212</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="electroconvulsive-therapy-ect">ELECTROCONVULSIVE THERAPY (ECT)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#electroconvulsive-therapy-ect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
213</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="electroconvulsive-therapy-ect">ELECTROCONVULSIVE THERAPY (ECT)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#electroconvulsive-therapy-ect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Involves application of electrodes to the head of the client to deliver an electrical impulse to the brain; this causes a seizure</li>
<li>It is believed that the shock stimulates brain chemistry to correct the chemical imbalance of depression</li>
<li>However, the mechanism of action of ECT is unclear at present</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
214</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="facts-about-electroconvulsive-therapy-ect">FACTS ABOUT ELECTROCONVULSIVE THERAPY (ECT)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#facts-about-electroconvulsive-therapy-ect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Voltage of electrical current that is administered to the client</li>
<li>70 – 150 volts</li>
<li>Length of electrical shock applied to the patient</li>
<li>About 0.5 to 2.0 seconds</li>
<li>Usual number of treatments needed to produce a therapeutic effect</li>
<li>6 – 12 treatments</li>
<li>Frequency of treatments</li>
<li>There should be an interval of 48 hours for each treatment</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
215</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="facts-about-electroconvulsive-therapy-ect">FACTS ABOUT ELECTROCONVULSIVE THERAPY (ECT)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#facts-about-electroconvulsive-therapy-ect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Indicators of effectiveness of ECT</li>
<li>The occurrence of generalized tonic-clonic seizure</li>
<li>Indications for ECT</li>
<li>Depression, Mania, Catatonic Schizophrenia</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
216</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="facts-about-electroconvulsive-therapy-ect">FACTS ABOUT ELECTROCONVULSIVE THERAPY (ECT)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#facts-about-electroconvulsive-therapy-ect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Contraindications to ECT</li>
<li>Fever</li>
<li>Increased intracranial tumor</li>
<li>TB with history of hemorrhage</li>
<li>Cardiac condition</li>
<li>Recent fracture</li>
<li>Retinal detachment</li>
<li>Pregnancy</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
217</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="facts-about-electroconvulsive-therapy-ect">FACTS ABOUT ELECTROCONVULSIVE THERAPY (ECT)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#facts-about-electroconvulsive-therapy-ect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Need for consent prior to ECT</li>
<li>Yes, consent is needed</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
218</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="facts-about-electroconvulsive-therapy-ect">FACTS ABOUT ELECTROCONVULSIVE THERAPY (ECT)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#facts-about-electroconvulsive-therapy-ect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Medications given to clients prior to ECT</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Atropine sulfate</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To decrease secretions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Anectine (Succinylcholine)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To promote muscle relaxation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Methohexital Sodium (Brevital)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Serves as an anesthetic agent</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
219</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="facts-about-electroconvulsive-therapy-ect">FACTS ABOUT ELECTROCONVULSIVE THERAPY (ECT)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#facts-about-electroconvulsive-therapy-ect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Common complications of ECT</li>
<li>Loss of memory</li>
<li>Headache</li>
<li>Apnea</li>
<li>Fracture</li>
<li>Respiratory depression</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
220</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-psychotherapeutic-interventions">COMMON PSYCHOTHERAPEUTIC INTERVENTIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-psychotherapeutic-interventions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
