<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="obsessive-compulsive-disorder">OBSESSIVE-COMPULSIVE DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obsessive-compulsive-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Involves obsession (thoughts, impulses or images) that cause marked anxiety and/or compulsions (repetitive behaviors or mental acts) that attempt to neutralize anxiety.</li>
<li>Obsessions that lead to compulsions.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
299</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="obsessive-compulsive-disorder">OBSESSIVE-COMPULSIVE DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obsessive-compulsive-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>OBSESSIONS</th><th>COMPULSIONS</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>FEAR OF DIRT AND GERMS</td><td>EXCESSIVE HAND WASHING</td></tr><tr><td>FEAR OF BURGLARY OR ROBBERY</td><td>REPEATED CHECKING OF DOOR AND WINDOW LOCKS</td></tr><tr><td>WORRIES ABOUT DISCARDING SOMETHING IMPORTANT</td><td>COUNTING AND RECOUNTING OF OBJECTS IN EVERYDAY LIFE</td></tr><tr><td>WORRIES THAT THINGS MUST BE SYMMETRICAL OR MATCHING</td><td>EXCESSIVE STRAIGHTENING, ORDERING, OR ARRANGING OF THINGS</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
301</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-obsessive-compulsive-disorder">MANAGEMENT OF OBSESSIVE-COMPULSIVE DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-obsessive-compulsive-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Anti-anxiety medications</li>
<li>Response prevention (delaying or avoiding performance of the rituals)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
302</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="generalized-anxiety-disorder">GENERALIZED ANXIETY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#generalized-anxiety-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Is characterized by at least six months of persistent and excessive worry and anxiety that interferes with a person's life</li>
<li>It is also characterized by motor tension, autonomic hyperactivity and cognitive vigilance</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
303</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="symptoms-of-generalized-anxiety-disorder">SYMPTOMS OF GENERALIZED ANXIETY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms-of-generalized-anxiety-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Apprehensive expectations more days than not for 6 months or more about several events or activities</li>
<li>Uncontrollable worrying</li>
<li>Significant distress or impaired social or occupational functioning</li>
<li>Three of the following symptoms:</li>
<li>Restlessness</li>
<li>Easily fatigued</li>
<li>Difficulty concentrating or mood going blank</li>
<li>Irritability</li>
<li>Muscle tension</li>
<li>Sleep disturbance</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
304</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-generalized-anxiety-disorder">MANAGEMENT OF GENERALIZED ANXIETY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-generalized-anxiety-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Anti-anxiety medications</li>
<li>Anti-depressants</li>
<li>Psychotherapy</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
305</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="acute-stress-disorder">ACUTE STRESS DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute-stress-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Is the development of anxiety, dissociative, and other symptoms within 1 month of exposure to an extremely traumatic stressor</li>
<li>It lasts 2 days to 4 weeks</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
306</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-acute-stress-disorder">MANAGEMENT OF ACUTE STRESS DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-acute-stress-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Anti-anxiety medications</li>
<li>Anti-depressant medications</li>
<li>Group therapy</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
308</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="post-traumatic-stress-disorder">POST-TRAUMATIC STRESS DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#post-traumatic-stress-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Is characterized by the re-experiencing of an extremely traumatic event, avoidance of stimuli associated with the event, numbing of responsiveness, and persistent increased arousal</li>
<li>It begins within 3 months to years after the event and may last a few months or years</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
309</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="symptoms-of-post-traumatic-stress-disorder">SYMPTOMS OF POST-TRAUMATIC STRESS DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#symptoms-of-post-traumatic-stress-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Exposure to traumatic event involving intense fear, helplessness or horror</li>
<li>Re-experiencing (intrusive recollections or dreams, flashbacks, physical and psychological distress over reminders of the event)</li>
<li>Avoidance of memory-provoking stimuli and numbing of general responsiveness (avoidance of thoughts, feelings, conversations, people, places, amnesia, diminished interest or participation in life events, feeling detached or estranged from others, restricted affect, sense of foreboding)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
310</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-post-traumatic-stress-disorder">MANAGEMENT OF POST-TRAUMATIC STRESS DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-post-traumatic-stress-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Anti-anxiety medications</li>
<li>Anti-depressant medications</li>
<li>Group therapy</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
311</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="personality-disorders">PERSONALITY DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personality-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
312</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="personality">PERSONALITY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personality" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It can be defined as an ingrained, enduring pattern of behaving and relating to self, others, and the environment; personality includes perceptions, attitudes, and emotions</li>
<li>These behaviors and characteristics are consistent across a broad range of situations and do not change easily</li>
<li>A person is usually not consciously aware of his personality</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
313</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="personality-disorders">PERSONALITY DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personality-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>These are personality styles that are rigid and maladaptive, causing significant personal distress and impair social functioning.</li>
<li>These are diagnosed when personality traits become inflexible and maladaptive and significantly interfere with how a person functions in society or cause the person emotional distress.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
314</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="etiological-factors">ETIOLOGICAL FACTORS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiological-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Genetic Factors</li>
<li>Due to inherited traits</li>
<li>Temperamental Factors</li>
<li>Due to emotional climate at home</li>
<li>Biological Factors</li>
<li>Due to imbalance in hormones and neurotransmitters</li>
<li>Psychoanalytic Factors</li>
<li>Due to fixation at certain psychosexual stage of development</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
315</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="personality-disorder-categories">PERSONALITY DISORDER CATEGORIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personality-disorder-categories" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Cluster A: Individuals whose behavior appears odd or eccentric (paranoid, schizoid, and schizotypal personality disorders)</li>
<li>Cluster B: Individuals who appear dramatic, emotional, or erratic (antisocial, borderline, histrionic, narcissistic)</li>
<li>Cluster C: Individuals who appear anxious or fearful (avoidant, dependent, obsessive-compulsive)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
316</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="paranoid-personality-disorder">PARANOID PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#paranoid-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms / Characteristics</li>
<li>Mistrust and suspicion of others</li>
<li>Guarded or hypervigilant and generally appear alert to any impending danger</li>
<li>Restricted affect</li>
<li>Mood is labile, quickly changing from quietly suspicious to angry or hostile</li>
<li>Responses become sarcastic for no apparent reason</li>
<li>Uses the defense mechanism of projection, which is blaming other people, institutions or events for their own difficulties</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
317</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="paranoid-personality-disorder">PARANOID PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#paranoid-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nursing Interventions</li>
<li>The nurse must be serious and straightforward with patient.</li>
<li>Involve the client in treatment planning</li>
<li>Because these clients need to feel in control, it is important to involve them in formulating plans of care.</li>
<li>The nurse asks what the client would like to accomplish in concrete terms.</li>
<li>Clients are more likely to engage in the therapeutic process if they believe they have something to gain</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
318</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="schizoid-personality-disorder">SCHIZOID PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#schizoid-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms / Characteristics</li>
<li>Detached from social relationships</li>
<li>They display a constricted affect and little, if any emotion; aloof and indifferent, appearing emotionally cold, uncaring, or unfeeling</li>
<li>Report no leisure or pleasurable activities because they rarely experience enjoyment</li>
<li>Have a pervasive lack of desire for involvement with others in all aspects of life</li>
<li>They do not have or desire friends, rarely date or marry and have little or no sexual contact</li>
<li>Involve themselves more with things than people</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
319</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="schizoid-personality-disorder">SCHIZOID PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#schizoid-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nursing Interventions</li>
<li>Focus on improved functioning of the client in the community</li>
<li>Assist the client to obtain essential services and health care, manage finances, etc.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
320</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="schizotypical-personality-disorder">SCHIZOTYPICAL PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#schizotypical-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms / Characteristics</li>
<li>Has social and interpersonal deficits marked by acute discomfort with and reduced capacity for close relationships</li>
<li>Has cognitive or perceptual distortions</li>
<li>Possesses eccentric behavior</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
321</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="schizotypal-personality-disorder">SCHIZOTYPAL PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#schizotypal-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nursing Interventions</li>
<li>Development of self-care skills</li>
<li>Nurse encourages client to establish a daily routine for hygiene and grooming</li>
<li>Improve community functioning and provide social skills training</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
322</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="antisocial-personality-disorder">ANTISOCIAL PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antisocial-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms / Characteristics</li>
<li>Violation of the rights of others</li>
<li>Lack of remorse for behavior</li>
<li>Shallow emotions</li>
<li>Lying</li>
<li>Rationalization of own behavior</li>
<li>Poor judgment</li>
<li>Impulsivity</li>
<li>Irritability and aggressiveness</li>
<li>Lack of insight</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
323</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="antisocial-personality-disorder">ANTISOCIAL PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antisocial-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nursing Interventions</li>
<li>Promote responsible behavior</li>
<li>Remind expectations.</li>
<li>Consistent adherence to rules and treatment plan</li>
<li>Confront the patient.</li>
<li>Decreasing and eliminating use of drugs and alcohol</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
324</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="borderline-personality-disorder">BORDERLINE PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#borderline-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms / Characteristics</li>
<li>Fear of abandonment, real or perceived</li>
<li>Unstable and intense relationships</li>
<li>Unstable self-image</li>
<li>Impulsivity or recklessness</li>
<li>Recurrent self-mutilating behavior or suicidal threats or gestures</li>
<li>Chronic feelings of emptiness and boredom</li>
<li>Labile mood</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
325</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="borderline-personality-disorder">BORDERLINE PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#borderline-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nursing Interventions:</li>
<li>Promote client's safety</li>
<li>The nurse must always seriously consider suicidal ideation with the presence of a plan, access to means for enacting the plan, and self-harm behaviors and institute appropriate action</li>
<li>The nurse can encourage clients to enter a no self-harm contract, in which a client promises to not engage in self-harm and to report to the nurse when he or she is losing control</li>
<li>The nurse emphasizes that the no self-harm contract is not a promise to the the nurse but is the client's promise to himself to be safe</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
326</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="borderline-personality-disorder">BORDERLINE PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#borderline-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nursing Interventions:</li>
<li>Helping clients to cope and control emotions</li>
<li>Clients often react to situations with extreme emotional responses without actually recognizing their feelings</li>
<li>The nurse can help clients to identify their feelings and learn to tolerate them without exaggerated responses such as destruction of property or self-harm</li>
<li>Keeping a journal often helps clients gain awareness of feelings.</li>
<li>The nurse can review journal entries as a basis for discussion</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
327</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="borderline-personality-disorder">BORDERLINE PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#borderline-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nursing Interventions:</li>
<li>Cognitive Restructuring Techniques</li>
<li>Helping clients to recognize negative thoughts and feeling and to replace them with positive patterns of thinking</li>
<li>Stop &amp; positive self talk.</li>
<li>Decatastrophizing</li>
<li>Occupation.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
328</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="histrionic-personality-disorder">HISTRIONIC PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#histrionic-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms / Characteristics</li>
<li>With a pervasive pattern of excessive emotionality and attention-seeking</li>
<li>Clients are overly concerned with impressing others with their appearance</li>
<li>Dress and flirtatious behavior are not limited to social situations or relationships but also occur in occupational and professional settings</li>
<li>Clients are extroverts</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
329</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="histrionic-personality-disorder">HISTRIONIC PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#histrionic-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms / Characteristics</li>
<li>Clients experience rapid shifts in mood and emotions and may be laughing uproaringly one moment and sobbing the next.</li>
<li>Thus their display of emotion may seem phony or forced on observers</li>
<li>Clients are uncomfortable when they are not the center of attention and go to great lengths to gain that status</li>
<li>Clients embarrass family members or friends by their flamboyant hugging, kissing of someone newly introduced, by sobbing over minor incidents</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
330</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="histrionic-personality-disorder">HISTRIONIC PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#histrionic-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nursing Interventions:</li>
<li>The nurse gives clients feedback about their social interactions with others including manner of dress and nonverbal behavior.</li>
<li>Feedback should focus on appropriate alternatives not merely criticism.</li>
<li>Teaching social skills and role-playing those skills in a safe, non-threatening environment can help clients to gain confidence in their ability to interact socially.</li>
<li>Encouraging clients to use assertive communication, such as "I" statements, may promote self-esteem and help them to get their needs met more appropriately.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
331</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="narcissistic-personality-disorder">NARCISSISTIC PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#narcissistic-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms / Characteristics</li>
<li>Has a pervasive pattern of grandiosity (in fantasy or behavior), need for admiration, and lack of empathy for others</li>
<li>They believe that they are superior, special and they demand special attention</li>
<li>They display an arrogant or haughty attitude</li>
<li>They view their problems as the fault of others</li>
<li>Underlying self-esteem is almost always fragile and vulnerable</li>
<li>They are hypersensitive to criticism and need constant attention, admiration</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
332</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="narcissistic-personality-disorder">NARCISSISTIC PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#narcissistic-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-interventions">Nursing Interventions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-interventions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The nurse must use self-awareness skills to avoid the anger and frustration that their behavior and attitude can engender</p>
<p>Clients may be rude and arrogant, unwilling to wait, and harsh and critical of the nurse. The nurse must not internalize such criticism or take it personally</p>
<p>The goal is to gain cooperation of these clients with other treatment as indicate</p>
<p>Teach expected behavior.</p>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
333</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="avoidant-personality-disorder">AVOIDANT PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#avoidant-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms / Characteristics</li>
<li>Has a pervasive pattern of social discomfort and reticence, low self-esteem and hypersensitivity to negative evaluation</li>
<li>They fear rejection, criticism, shame or disapproval</li>
<li>They remain aloof in their relationships and feel inferior to others</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
334</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="avoidant-personality-disorder">AVOIDANT PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#avoidant-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nursing Interventions:</li>
<li>These clients require much support and reassurance from the nurse</li>
<li>The nurse can help them to explore positive self-aspects, positive responses from others, and possible reasons for self-criticism</li>
<li>Helping clients to practice self-affirmations and positive self-talk may be useful in promoting self esteem</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
335</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dependent-personality-disorder">DEPENDENT PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dependent-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms / Characteristics</li>
<li>Has a pervasive and excessive need to be taken care of which leads to submissive and clinging behavior and fears of separation</li>
<li>Has incessant demands for attention from others, lacks self-confidence, needs excessive reassurance and advice</li>
<li>They are pre-occupied with excessive fears of being left alone to care for themselves</li>
<li>They perceive themselves as unable to function outside a relationship with someone who can tell them what to do</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
336</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dependent-personality-disorder">DEPENDENT PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dependent-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nursing Interventions:</li>
<li>The nurse must help the clients to express feelings of grief and loss over the end of a relationship while fostering autonomy and self reliance</li>
<li>Helping clients to identify their strengths and needs is more helpful than encouraging the overwhelming belief that the client can't do anything alone</li>
<li>Clients may need assistance in daily functioning like planning menus, shopping, budgeting money, etc.</li>
<li>The nurse teaches problem-solving and decision-making skills</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
337</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="obsessive-compulsive-personality-disorder">OBSESSIVE-COMPULSIVE PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obsessive-compulsive-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms / Characteristics</li>
<li>Has a pervasive pattern of preoccupation with perfectionism, mental and interpersonal control and orderliness at the expense of flexibility, openness and efficiency</li>
<li>They are formal, serious and answer questions with precision and much detail</li>
<li>Clients check and recheck the details of any project or activity</li>
<li>They have problems with judgment and decision-making — specifically actually reaching a decision</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
338</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="obsessive-compulsive-personality-disorder">OBSESSIVE-COMPULSIVE PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obsessive-compulsive-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Symptoms / Characteristics</li>
<li>They have low self-esteem and are always harsh, critical, and judgmental of themselves; they believe they “could have done better” regardless of how well the job has been done</li>
<li>They have difficulty in relationships, few friends, and little social life</li>
<li>They cannot tolerate lack of control</li>
<li>They have difficulty working collaboratively, preferring to “do it myself” so it is done correctly</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
339</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="obsessive-compulsive-personality-disorder">OBSESSIVE-COMPULSIVE PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obsessive-compulsive-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nursing Interventions:</li>
<li>Nurses may be able to help clients to view decision-making and completion of projects from a different perspective</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
340</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="obsessive-compulsive-personality-disorder">OBSESSIVE-COMPULSIVE PERSONALITY DISORDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obsessive-compulsive-personality-disorder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Nursing Interventions:</li>
<li>Use of cognitive restructuring techniques like decatastrophizing may challenge some rigid and inflexible thinking</li>
<li>Encouraging clients to take risks, such as letting someone else plan a family activity, may improve relationships</li>
<li>Practicing negotiation with family or friends may help them to relinquish some of their need for control</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
341</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="other-related-disorders">OTHER RELATED DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-related-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Depressive Personality Disorder</li>
<li>Passive Aggressive Personality Disorder</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
342</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="points-to-consider-when-working-with-clients-with-personality-disorders">POINTS TO CONSIDER WHEN WORKING WITH CLIENTS WITH PERSONALITY DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#points-to-consider-when-working-with-clients-with-personality-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Talking to colleagues about feelings of frustration will help you to deal with your emotional responses so you can be more effective with clients</li>
<li>Clear, frequent communication with other health care providers can help to diminish the client's manipulation</li>
<li>Do not take undue flattery or harsh criticism personally; it is a result of the client's personality disorder</li>
<li>Set realistic goals and remember that behavior changes in clients with personality disorders take a long time. Progress can be very slow</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
343</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="autism">AUTISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#autism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
344</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="autism">AUTISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#autism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Is a disorder characterized by impairment in communication skills, or the presence of stereotyped behavior, interests and activities with associated impairment in social interactions</li>
<li>More common among boys</li>
<li>Usually diagnosed at age 2</li>
<li>It is treatable but not curable</li>
<li>Impaired interpersonal functioning</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
345</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="most-acceptable-cause-of-autism">MOST ACCEPTABLE CAUSE OF AUTISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#most-acceptable-cause-of-autism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Biological Factors</li>
<li>Brain anoxia</li>
<li>Intake of drugs</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
346</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="most-common-signs-and-symptoms-of-autism">MOST COMMON SIGNS AND SYMPTOMS OF AUTISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#most-common-signs-and-symptoms-of-autism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Resist normal teaching method</li>
<li>Silly laughing or giggling</li>
<li>Echolalia</li>
<li>Acts as deaf</li>
<li>No fear of danger</li>
<li>Insensitive to pain</li>
<li>Crying tantrums</li>
<li>Loves to spin objects</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
347</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="most-common-signs-and-symptoms-of-autism">MOST COMMON SIGNS AND SYMPTOMS OF AUTISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#most-common-signs-and-symptoms-of-autism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Resists change in the routine</li>
<li>Sustained odd play</li>
<li>Difficulty interacting with others</li>
<li>No eye contact</li>
<li>Wants blocks and not balls</li>
<li>Points to anything</li>
<li>Attachment to inanimate objects</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
348</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-problems-and-appropriate-management">COMMON PROBLEMS AND APPROPRIATE MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-problems-and-appropriate-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Tantrums-Risk for injury</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Involves head-banging</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Place a helmet on the head</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Communication</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All vowels</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Use of short sentences when talking to the child</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Routines</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Provide consistency</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
349</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mental-retardation">MENTAL RETARDATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mental-retardation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
350</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mental-retardation">MENTAL RETARDATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mental-retardation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It is not a mental illness</li>
<li>Main problem is inadequate mental functioning</li>
<li>Essential feature of MR is below-average functioning (IQ less than 70) accompanied by significant limitations in areas of adaptive functioning.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
351</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="levels-of-mental-retardation">LEVELS OF MENTAL RETARDATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#levels-of-mental-retardation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>LEVEL OF MENTAL RETARDATION</th><th>INTELLIGENCE QUOTIENT (IQ)</th><th>WHAT CAN BE DONE</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>MILD / MORON</td><td>50 / 55 TO 70</td><td>EDUCABLE</td></tr><tr><td>MODERATE / IMBECILE</td><td>35 / 40 TO 50 / 55</td><td>TRAINABLE</td></tr><tr><td>SEVERE / IDIOT</td><td>20 / 25 TO 35 / 40</td><td>NEEDS CLOSE SUPERVISION</td></tr><tr><td>PROFOUND</td><td>BELOW 20 / 25</td><td>NEEDS CUSTODIAL CARE</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
352</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="basis-of-diagnosis-of-mental-retardation">BASIS OF DIAGNOSIS OF MENTAL RETARDATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basis-of-diagnosis-of-mental-retardation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The Intelligence Quotient should not be the only criterion used in making a diagnosis of Mental Retardation.</li>
<li>It should serve only to help in making a clinical judgment of the patient's adaptive behavioral capacity.</li>
<li>This judgment should also be based on an evaluation of the patient's developmental history and present functioning, social and emotional maturity.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
353</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-mental-retardation">CAUSES OF MENTAL RETARDATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-mental-retardation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Congenital numerical deficiency or abnormal arrangement of brain cells</li>
<li>Birth injuries due to pelvic disproportion, premature births or forceps delivery</li>
<li>Rh blood-factor incompatibility between mother and child</li>
<li>Infectious diseases, such as German measles of the mother during the first three months of pregnancy</li>
<li>Infectious diseases during childhood, such as meningitis and encephalitis</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
354</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-mental-retardation">CAUSES OF MENTAL RETARDATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-mental-retardation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Brain injuries occurring during childhood</li>
<li>Endocrine deficiencies, such as thyroid deficiency, known to be the cause of cretinism</li>
<li>Exposure to environmental deprivation, with poor housing and poor economic and social conditions.</li>
<li>Familial or hereditary causes</li>
<li>Inborn errors of metabolism, such as the inability to metabolize proteins, carbohydrates or fats.</li>
<li>Genetic defects, such as abnormalities in genes and chromosomes</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
355</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-of-mental-retardation">PREVENTION OF MENTAL RETARDATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-mental-retardation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Adequate medical care during the prenatal period and birth</li>
<li>Early detection of various disorders</li>
<li>Immunization against communicable diseases</li>
<li>Educating parents to understand the important concepts of growth and development</li>
<li>Educating family members and society to accept the mentally retarded</li>
<li>Better housing and living conditions</li>
<li>Improved nutrition through dietary requirement instruction and meal planning</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
356</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-mentally-retarded-patients">NURSING CARE FOR MENTALLY RETARDED PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-mentally-retarded-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Help parents accept a diagnosis of mental retardation</li>
<li>Consider the developmental or functional age and not the chronological age</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
357</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-mentally-retarded-patients">NURSING CARE FOR MENTALLY RETARDED PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-mentally-retarded-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Teach parents that they should:</li>
<li>Protect the child from danger</li>
<li>Make the child as independent as his condition will permit</li>
<li>Teach the child small social graces and manners which are a tremendous factor in helping to be accepted by others</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
358</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-mentally-retarded-patients">NURSING CARE FOR MENTALLY RETARDED PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-mentally-retarded-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Teach parents that they should:</li>
<li>Teach the child to refrain from holding their mouths open as this gives them a dull appearance</li>
<li>Select attractive, well-fitted clothing, hair style and good hygiene practices</li>
<li>Eliminate the child's undesirable social traits, such as touching their noses and ears, scratching, etc.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
359</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-mentally-retarded-patients">NURSING CARE FOR MENTALLY RETARDED PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-mentally-retarded-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Teach parents that they should:</li>
<li>Teach the child only one thing at a time</li>
<li>Demonstrate what they teach, whenever possible</li>
<li>Use pictures, since these are valuable visual aids</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
360</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-mentally-retarded-patients">NURSING CARE FOR MENTALLY RETARDED PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-mentally-retarded-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Teach parents that they should:</li>
<li>Start teaching the child simple things, gradually progressing to more complex learning experiences</li>
<li>Remember that patience and repetition are necessary virtues</li>
<li>Avoid prolonged teaching sessions since retarded individuals easily become fatigued</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
361</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-mentally-retarded-patients">NURSING CARE FOR MENTALLY RETARDED PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-mentally-retarded-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Teach parents that they should:</li>
<li>Refrain from scolding because it blocks learning and instills fear</li>
<li>Give compliments as a motivating force</li>
<li>Not show fear themselves as this emotion will be transferred to the child</li>
<li>Protect the child from teasing and taunting</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
362</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-mentally-retarded-patients">NURSING CARE FOR MENTALLY RETARDED PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-mentally-retarded-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Teach parents that they should:</li>
<li>Recognize a temper tantrum as a child's attempt to meet some underlying emotional need such as attention, affection and security or as the expression of the child's dislike for activity</li>
<li>Recognize that these children have a tendency to express jealousy</li>
<li>Know that play activities are enjoyed and may be a teaching experience.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
363</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="principles-of-nursing-care-for-mentally-retarded-patients">PRINCIPLES OF NURSING CARE FOR MENTALLY RETARDED PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-nursing-care-for-mentally-retarded-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Repetition</li>
<li>Role Modeling</li>
<li>Restructuring the Environment</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="focus-of-education-for-mentally-retarded-patients">FOCUS OF EDUCATION FOR MENTALLY RETARDED PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#focus-of-education-for-mentally-retarded-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="attention-deficit-hyperactivity-disorder-adhd">ATTENTION DEFICIT HYPERACTIVITY DISORDER (ADHD)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#attention-deficit-hyperactivity-disorder-adhd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="attention-deficit-hyperactivity-disorder-adhd">ATTENTION DEFICIT HYPERACTIVITY DISORDER (ADHD)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#attention-deficit-hyperactivity-disorder-adhd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A disorder characterized by:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inattentiveness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Over-activity</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Impulsiveness</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A common disorder among boys</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Occurs before the age of 7</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
367</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="main-problems-in-adhd">MAIN PROBLEMS IN ADHD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#main-problems-in-adhd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-etiological-factors">COMMON ETIOLOGICAL FACTORS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-etiological-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="signs-and-symptoms-of-adhd">SIGNS AND SYMPTOMS OF ADHD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms-of-adhd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Subdivided into:</li>
<li>Inattentive behaviors</li>
<li>Hyperactive and Impulsive behaviors</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
370</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="signs-and-symptoms-of-adhd-inattentive-behaviors">SIGNS AND SYMPTOMS OF ADHD - INATTENTIVE BEHAVIORS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms-of-adhd-inattentive-behaviors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Misses details</li>
<li>Makes careless mistakes</li>
<li>Has difficulty sustaining attention</li>
<li>Does not seem to listen</li>
<li>Does not follow-through on chores or homework</li>
<li>Has difficulty with organization</li>
<li>Avoids tasks requiring mental effort</li>
<li>Often loses necessary things</li>
<li>Is easily distracted by other stimuli</li>
<li>Is often forgetful in daily activities</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
371</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="signs-and-symptoms-of-adhd-hyperactive-impulsive-behaviours">SIGNS AND SYMPTOMS OF ADHD - HYPERACTIVE / IMPULSIVE BEHAVIOURS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms-of-adhd-hyperactive-impulsive-behaviours" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Fidgets</li>
<li>Often leaves a seat, (e.g., during a meal)</li>
<li>Runs or climbs excessively</li>
<li>Can not play quietly</li>
<li>Is always on the go; driven</li>
<li>Talks excessively</li>
<li>Blurts out answers</li>
<li>Interrupts</li>
<li>Can't wait for turn</li>
<li>Is intrusive with siblings and playmates</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
372</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="psychopharmacology-for-adhd">PSYCHOPHARMACOLOGY FOR ADHD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychopharmacology-for-adhd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Stimulant Drugs</li>
<li>Methylphenidate (Ritalin) – drug of choice</li>
<li>Dextroamphetamine (Dexedrine)</li>
<li>Amphetamine (Adderall)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
373</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-adhd">NURSING CARE FOR ADHD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-adhd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Ensuring the client's safety and that of others</li>
<li>Stop unsafe behavior (priority nursing diagnosis is RISK FOR INJURY)</li>
<li>Provide close supervision</li>
<li>Give clear directions about acceptable and unacceptable behavior</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
374</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-adhd">NURSING CARE FOR ADHD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-adhd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Improved role performance</li>
<li>Give positive feedback for meeting expectations</li>
<li>Manage the environment (e.g., provide a quiet place free of distractions for task completion)</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
375</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-adhd">NURSING CARE FOR ADHD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-adhd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<li>Simplifying instructions and directions</li>
<li>Get the child's full attention</li>
<li>Break complex tasks into small steps</li>

</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
376</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-adhd">NURSING CARE FOR ADHD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-adhd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
