<p>To patient's embarrassments.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Client's choice of social support.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Visit:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><a href="http://www.scie.ca/helpcard.htm" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">www.scie.ca/helpcard.htm</a> for more information.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
573</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="organic-mental-disorders">ORGANIC MENTAL DISORDERS.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organic-mental-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A mental or behavioural abnormality related to the dysfunction of the brain.</li>
<li>delirium.</li>
<li>Alzheimer's disease.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
574</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="alzheimer-s-disease">ALZHEIMER'S DISEASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#alzheimer-s-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A chronic, progressive condition that is the major cause of degenerative dementia seen in the elderly</li>
<li>The main pathology is the presence of senile plaques that destroys neurons leading to decreased acetylcholine</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
575</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="4as-of-alzheimer-s-disease">4As OF ALZHEIMER'S DISEASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4as-of-alzheimer-s-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Aphasia</li>
<li>Loss of language ability</li>
<li>Apraxia</li>
<li>Loss of purposeful movement without loss of muscle power or coordination in general</li>
<li>Agnosia</li>
<li>Loss of sensory ability to recognize objects</li>
<li>Amnesia</li>
<li>Mnemonic disturbances or memory loss</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
576</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="predisposing-factors-in-alzheimer-s-disease">PREDISPOSING FACTORS IN ALZHEIMER'S DISEASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors-in-alzheimer-s-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Genetics</li>
<li>In 10% to 20%, runs in the family</li>
<li>Viral</li>
<li>Aluminum</li>
<li>Vitamin B12 deficiency</li>
<li>Related with Down's syndrome</li>
<li>Possible defect in the immune system</li>
<li>Disrupted biochemical pathways and other metabolic (glucose) abnormalities</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
577</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-alzheimer-s-patients">NURSING CARE FOR ALZHEIMER'S PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-alzheimer-s-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Promote normal motor behavior</li>
<li>Living areas must be well lit and furniture left in the same place</li>
<li>Safety bars installed near toilets, showers, and tubs</li>
<li>Teach safe use of walkers and wheelchairs</li>
<li>Evaluate clients using tranquilizers and antidepressants for postural hypotension</li>
<li>Avoid crowds or large open spaces without boundaries</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
579</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-alzheimer-s-patients">NURSING CARE FOR ALZHEIMER'S PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-alzheimer-s-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Maintain self-care</li>
<li>Allow the client to do as much as possible unassisted</li>
<li>Remind client about daily grooming</li>
<li>Remind client about grooming and personal hygiene</li>
<li>Use mouth swabs with dilute hydrogen peroxide if client resists mouth care</li>
<li>Total bed care</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
580</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-alzheimer-s-patients">NURSING CARE FOR ALZHEIMER'S PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-alzheimer-s-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Promote adequate sleep</li>
<li>Allow sleepless clients to wander in a confined area until they are tired</li>
<li>Make sure room is lighted and without shadows</li>
<li>Leave a radio on to provide more stimulation</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
581</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-alzheimer-s-patients">NURSING CARE FOR ALZHEIMER'S PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-alzheimer-s-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Promote optimal patterns of elimination</li>
<li>Toileting routine is essential</li>
<li>Promote optimal nutritional status</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
582</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-alzheimer-s-patients">NURSING CARE FOR ALZHEIMER'S PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-alzheimer-s-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Support knowledge processes</li>
<li>Support optimal verbal expression</li>
<li>Call the client by name, approach in a clear view and give simple directions</li>
<li>Support optimal role performance</li>
<li>Client must be viewed as an active family member</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
583</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-alzheimer-s-patients">NURSING CARE FOR ALZHEIMER'S PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-alzheimer-s-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Support optimal memory function</li>
<li>Gently orient client</li>
<li>Do not argue about verbal discrepancies. Rather, direct client towards areas of interest that are familiar and pleasurable</li>
<li>Music therapy</li>
<li>Drug therapy</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
584</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-alzheimer-s-patients">NURSING CARE FOR ALZHEIMER'S PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-alzheimer-s-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Promote optimal orientation</li>
<li>Structure environment to support cognition</li>
<li>Hearing or visual aids are necessary to prevent sensory loss or distortion</li>
<li>Easy to read clocks, orientation boards and consistent daily routine</li>
<li>Do not quiz the client</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
585</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-for-alzheimer-s-patients">NURSING CARE FOR ALZHEIMER'S PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-for-alzheimer-s-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Support appropriate conduct or impulse control</li>
<li>Client functions best in an environment where stimulation is controlled and sensory overload is prevented</li>
<li>Changes must be done slowly</li>
<li>Call client by name, approach in full view and refrain from touching client</li>
<li>Requests should be simple and non-demanding</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
586</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="delirium">Delirium.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#delirium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A disturbance in consciousness and a change in cognition that develops over a short period of time.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If identified earlier, it is usually reversible.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clinical hallmarks:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Decreased attention span.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>On and off confusion.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
587</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="delirium">Delirium.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#delirium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Diagnostic criteria:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disturbance of consciousness.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Memory deficit.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disorientation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Altered diurnal patterns.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Perceptual disturbances.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Occurs in:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>30% in hospitalized cancer patients.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>80% near death.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
588</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes">Causes.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Medications.</li>
<li>Hypoxia.</li>
<li>Hypoglycemia.</li>
<li>Hyperthermia.</li>
<li>Alcohol withdrawal.</li>
<li>Infections.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
589</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">Nursing Management.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Identify the cause followed by;</li>
<li>Elimination of the cause.</li>
<li>Supportive management.</li>
<li>Offer good nursing care:</li>
<li>Vital signs.</li>
<li>Behaviour.</li>
<li>Mental status monitoring.</li>
<li>Protect the patient from physical injury- use low beds, guard rails.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
590</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">Nursing Management.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Assist in needs related to nutrition.</li>
<li>Maintain hazard free environment.</li>
<li>Remove stimuli that cause misperception.</li>
<li>Maintain a well lit environment</li>
<li>Administer drugs as ordered.</li>
<li>Reorient the patient.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
591</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>INDICATOR</th><th>DELIRIUM</th><th>DEMENTIA</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Onset</td><td>Rapid</td><td>Gradual and insidious</td></tr><tr><td>Duration</td><td>Brief (hours to days)</td><td>Progressive deterioration</td></tr><tr><td>Level of Consciousness</td><td>Impaired, fluctuates</td><td>Not affected</td></tr><tr><td>Memory</td><td>Short-term memory impaired</td><td>Short-term then Long-term memory impaired, eventually destroyed</td></tr><tr><td>Speech</td><td>May be slurred,rambling, pressured, irrelevant</td><td>Normal in early stage, progressive aphasia in later stage</td></tr><tr><td>Thought Processes</td><td>Temporarily disorganized</td><td>Impaired thinking, eventual loss of thinking abilities</td></tr><tr><td>Perception</td><td>Visual or tactile hallucinations, delusions</td><td>Often absent, but can have paranoia, hallucinations, illusions</td></tr><tr><td>Mood</td><td>Anxious, fearful if hallucinating; weeping, irritable</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Mr. Vincent Ejakait</td><td>Depressed and anxious in early stage, labile mood, restless pacing, angry out-bursts in later stages</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>592</td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="alcoholism">ALCOHOLISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#alcoholism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
593</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="alcohol">Alcohol<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#alcohol" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>ETHANOL (CH₃CH₂OH)</p>
<p>Alcohol dehydrogenase</p>
<p>ACETALDEHYDE (CH₃CHO)</p>
<p>Aldehyde dehydrogenase</p>
<p>ACETYL COENZYME A</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>α</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\alpha</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4306em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.0037em;">α</span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p>energy</p>

<p>carbon dioxide</p>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait</p>

<p>water</p>
<p>594</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="alcoholism">ALCOHOLISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#alcoholism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>WHO definition:</li>
<li>A chronic disease or a disorder characterized by excessive alcohol intake and interference in the individual's health, interpersonal relationship and economic functioning</li>
<li>Considered to be present when there is 0.1% or 10 ml for every 1,000 ml of blood</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
595</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dynamics-of-alcoholism">DYNAMICS OF ALCOHOLISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dynamics-of-alcoholism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Social drinking may progress to abuse.</li>
<li>Alcohol being a depressant aids in the relaxing of the individual and releases inhibitions.</li>
<li>Screening for alcoholism:</li>
<li>CAGE.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
596</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="phases-of-progression-of-alcoholism">PHASES OF PROGRESSION OF ALCOHOLISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#phases-of-progression-of-alcoholism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Pre-alcoholic Phase</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Starts with social drinking until tolerance begins to develop</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Prodromal Phase</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Alcohol becomes a need; blackouts occur; denial begins to develop</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Crucial Phase</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Cardinal symptoms of alcoholism develops (loss of control over drinking)</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Chronic Phase</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>The person becomes intoxicated all day</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
597</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="manifestations-of-different-blood-levels-of-alcohol">MANIFESTATIONS OF DIFFERENT BLOOD LEVELS OF ALCOHOL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#manifestations-of-different-blood-levels-of-alcohol" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>BLOOD LEVEL</th><th>MANIFESTATION</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>0.1% TO 0.2%</td><td>Low coordination</td></tr><tr><td>0.2% TO 0.3%</td><td>Presence of ataxia, tremors, irritability, stupor</td></tr><tr><td>0.3% and above</td><td>Unconsciousness</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
598</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="effects-of-alcohol">EFFECTS OF ALCOHOL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-alcohol" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>If taken in exceedingly high doses, it can depress respiration and cause death.</li>
<li>Intoxication occurs when a person's blood alcohol level is 0.10% or more</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
599</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="effects-of-alcohol">EFFECTS OF ALCOHOL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-alcohol" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Simple intoxication lasts less than 12 hours and is usually followed by a hangover occurring approximately 4 – 6 hours after alcohol ingestion.</li>
<li>The cause is uncertain: ?</li>
<li>Hypoglycemia</li>
<li>the accumulation of lactic acid and acetaldehyde in the blood.</li>
<li>Alcoholic hallucinosis</li>
<li>Auditory hallucinations reported approximately 48 hours after heavy drinking.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
600</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="possible-outcomes-of-alcoholism">POSSIBLE OUTCOMES OF ALCOHOLISM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#possible-outcomes-of-alcoholism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Brain damage</li>
<li>Alcoholic hallucinosis</li>
<li>Death</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
601</p>

<li>Domineering</li>

<p>5Ds</p>

602</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-defense-mechanisms-utilized-by-alcoholics">COMMON DEFENSE MECHANISMS UTILIZED BY ALCOHOLICS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-defense-mechanisms-utilized-by-alcoholics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stages-of-alcohol-withdrawal-syndrome">STAGES OF ALCOHOL WITHDRAWAL SYNDROME<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-alcohol-withdrawal-syndrome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-tremulousness">1) Tremulousness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-tremulousness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Occurs during the drinking period up to 2 hours afterwards.</li>
<li>There is anxiety, agitation and irritability</li>
<li>As it progresses, tremors, tachycardia and diaphoresis are exhibited</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
604</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stages-of-alcohol-withdrawal-syndrome">STAGES OF ALCOHOL WITHDRAWAL SYNDROME<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-alcohol-withdrawal-syndrome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-hallucinations">2) Hallucinations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-hallucinations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Begins 12 – 48 hours after the person stops drinking</li>
<li>Gastrointestinal symptoms of nausea, vomiting, diarrhea and anorexia are present</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
605</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stages-of-alcohol-withdrawal-syndrome">STAGES OF ALCOHOL WITHDRAWAL SYNDROME<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-alcohol-withdrawal-syndrome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="delirium-tremens">Delirium tremens<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#delirium-tremens" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A condition of severe memory disturbance, agitation, anorexia and hallucinations</li>
<li>Begins a few days after drinking stops and ends within 1 – 5 days</li>
<li>There is elevated temperature, severe diaphoresis, hypertension and tachycardia</li>
<li>Behavioral symptoms include confusion with disorientation, agitation, tremors, and alterations in sensory perception.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
606</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-withdrawal-signs-and-symptoms">COMMON WITHDRAWAL SIGNS AND SYMPTOMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-withdrawal-signs-and-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hallucinations (visual and tactile)</li>
<li>Increased vital signs</li>
<li>Tremors</li>
<li>Sweating and seizures</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
607</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-withdrawal">COMMON WITHDRAWAL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-withdrawal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="syndromes-experienced-by">SYNDROMES EXPERIENCED BY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#syndromes-experienced-by" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="alcoholics">ALCOHOLICS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#alcoholics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>SYNDROME</th><th>CAUSE</th><th>ONSET</th><th>ESSENTIAL FEATURE</th><th>OTHER SIGNS AND SYMPTOMS</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>DELIRIUM TREMENS</td><td>Faulty metabolism of alcohol</td><td>Acute</td><td>Delirium</td><td>Increased vital signs</td></tr><tr><td>Visual and tactile hallucinations</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Coarse tremors</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>KORSAKOFF'S PSYCHOSIS</td><td>Thiamine and Niacin deficiency</td><td>Chronic</td><td>Memory Disturbances</td><td>Retrograde amnesia</td></tr><tr><td>Anterograde amnesia</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Confabulation</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>WERNICKE'S PSYCHOSIS</td><td>Thiamine deficiency</td><td>Chronic</td><td></td><td>Confusion</td></tr><tr><td>Opthalmoplegia</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Ataxia</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
608</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pharmacologic-treatment-of-alcoholic-patients">PHARMACOLOGIC TREATMENT OF ALCOHOLIC PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pharmacologic-treatment-of-alcoholic-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Vitamin B1 (Thiamine):</li>
<li>is often prescribed to prevent or to treat Wernicke's syndrome and Korsakoff's syndrome, which are neurologic conditions that can result from heavy alcohol use.</li>
<li>Alcohol withdrawal is managed with a benzodiazepine anxiolytic agent, which is used to suppress the symptoms of abstinence.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
609</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pharmacologic-treatment-of-alcoholic-patients">PHARMACOLOGIC TREATMENT OF ALCOHOLIC PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pharmacologic-treatment-of-alcoholic-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Disulfiram (Antabuse) may be prescribed to help deter clients from drinking.</li>
<li>If a client taking disulfiram drinks alcohol, a severe adverse reaction occurs with flushing, a throbbing headache, sweating, nausea and vomiting.</li>
<li>In severe cases, severe hypotension, confusion, coma, and even death may result</li>
<li>The client must avoid a wide variety of products that contain alcohol such as cough syrup, lotions, mouthwash, perfume, aftershave, vinegar and vanilla and other extracts.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
610</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>DRUG</th><th>USE</th><th>DOSAGE</th><th>NURSING CONSIDERATIONS</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Lorazepam (Ativan)</td><td>Alcohol withdrawal</td><td>2 – 4 mg every 2 – 4 hours prn</td><td>Monitor vital signs and global assessments for effectiveness; may cause dizziness and drowsiness</td></tr><tr><td>Chlordiazepoxide (Librium)</td><td>Alcohol withdrawal</td><td>50-100 mg, repeat in 2-4 hours if necessary, not to exceed 300 mg/day</td><td>Monitor vital signs and global assessments for effectiveness; may cause dizziness and drowsiness</td></tr><tr><td>Disulfiram (Antabuse)</td><td>Maintain abstinence from alcohol</td><td>500 mg/day for 1-2 weeks, then 250 mg/day</td><td>Teach client to read labels to avoid products with alcohol</td></tr><tr><td>Thiamine (Vitamin B1)</td><td>Prevent or treat Wernicke, Korsakoff syn</td><td>100 mg/day</td><td>Teach client about proper nutrition</td></tr><tr><td>Folic Acid (folate)</td><td>Treat nutritional deficiencies</td><td>1 – 2 mg/day</td><td>Teach client about proper nutrition; Urine may be dark yellow</td></tr><tr><td>Cyanocobalamin (Vitamin B12)</td><td>For nutritional deficiencies</td><td>25 – 250 mcg/day</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Mr. Vincent Ejakait</td><td>Teach client about nutrition</td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-interventions-for-alcoholic-patients">NURSING INTERVENTIONS FOR ALCOHOLIC PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-interventions-for-alcoholic-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Using confrontation strategies</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Teach the client the consequences of alcohol;</li>
<li>Job loss.</li>
<li>Poor health.</li>
<li>Poverty.</li>
<li>Family breakup.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
612</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-interventions-for-alcoholic-patients">NURSING INTERVENTIONS FOR ALCOHOLIC PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-interventions-for-alcoholic-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>Make use of educating video tapes and talks by recovered alcoholics</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Referral and self-help groups</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
613</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-interventions-for-alcoholic-patients">NURSING INTERVENTIONS FOR ALCOHOLIC PATIENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-interventions-for-alcoholic-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol start="5">
<li>Encourage lifestyle changes.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Nurses can help clients discuss ways to alter their destructive habits by suggesting different coping strategies and by encouraging clients to discover new interests and capabilities within themselves.</li>
<li>Recognizing that relapses are always a threat, nurses may set up contracts with the client.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
614</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cannabis-marijuana">CANNABIS-MARIJUANA.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cannabis-marijuana" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<li>Usually smoked.</li>

<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251224-b2bfb098.jpeg" alt="img-29.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>Causes:</li>

<li>Active ingredient is THC.</li>
<li>Hashish is the resin found in flowers of mature C.sativae.</li>
<li>Long term use leads to accumulation in the body.</li>
<li>Marihuana, marijuana, bhang, ganja, hashish or charas, sinsemilla, red oil.</li>
</ul>

Pharmacology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-pharmacology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>

<li>Cocaine-HCl is injected I.V. =&gt; “rush” or “flash” =&gt; euphoria.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cocaine">Cocaine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cocaine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a. <strong>Acute effects</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><strong>CNS stimulation.</strong>
Increase alertness, feeling of elation and well being, increased energy, feelings of competence, increased sexuality.</li>
</ul>
<p>The user becomes more <strong>talkative, restless and often more irritable</strong>. Consciousness is clear, but delusions may occur as well as visual, tactile (formication) and auditory hallucinations.</p>
<p>These drugs are <strong>sympathomimetic</strong>.</p>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
619</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-overdose">Treatment of overdose<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-overdose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Beta blockers =&gt; for autonomic hyperactivity.</li>
<li>Nitroglycerine or other nitrites/nitrates → for angina.</li>
<li>Calcium channel blockers → for hypertension.</li>
<li>Ice baths → for high fever.</li>
<li>Acidify urine → to hasten excretion.</li>
<li>Monitor vital signs.</li>
<li>Psychotherapy.</li>
<li>Health education.</li>
<li>Antidepressants → for depression</li>
<li>Haloperidol → for psychosis.</li>
<li>Alprazolam → for panic attacks.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-acute-effects">a. Acute Effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-acute-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-acute-intoxication">B. Acute Intoxication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-acute-intoxication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Respiratory arrest due to blockade of respiratory centers and neuromuscular junctions controlling breathing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-chronic-effects">C. Chronic effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-chronic-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Associated diseases: Heart disease, lung disease, cancer, babies with small birth weight, asthma in children, others.</p>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
625</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assignment">Assignment.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Read about:</li>
<li>The concept of loss</li>
<li>Stages of grief and nursing management.</li>
<li>Nursing management of violent patient.</li>
<li>Khat.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
626</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="psychiatric-assessment">Psychiatric assessment.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychiatric-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>History taking should include a thorough psychological assessment.</li>
<li>This is followed by a MSE.</li>
<li>Maintain privacy for the client.</li>
<li>Establish a rapport with the client.</li>
<li>Make sure you and the patient are seated near the door.</li>
<li>Introduce yourself and give the pt. an estimate of the time the interview will take.</li>
<li>If the patient is anxious, CALM him/her</li>
</ul>
<p>Mr. Vincent Ejakait
634</p>
